< Review>
Great ribeye steaks and happy hour appetizers!  The clam chowder is delicious.  It has the perfect balance of potatoes and clams.  The real clam broth brings it to perfection.  The seafood Fra Diavlo is very good and my wife's go to order.  I love their ribeye steak with the peppercorn sauce.  The sauce is the perfect complement to the juicy tender steak.  The servers aim to please,are  very attentive, and gladly provide recommendations if you can't decide what to order.  All in all an excellent dining experience.<//Review>

We should have come sooner. I don't know why we have never tried eating at Point Loma Cafe before. I drive past it all the time but I never pulled in to try it. What a mistake that was! Inside is clean, spacious and nicely decorated. The food was unexpectedly tasty and our waitress, Bing, was a delightful lady who we hope serves us again next time. <date>1560677821520</date><Name>Vishwesh Rege</Name><resp>None</resp><Pics>None< /Pics><review>Apparently the actual Point Loma Cafe closes at 130pm daily, after which you need to visit the Bayside Bar at the backside, which has the same menu. This is a comfortable spot with an outside pool and garden. The overall food and service is pretty good. Staff is friendly and welcoming. We ordered the spicy chicken wings, which had a spicy sour flavor, and the sauteed chicken breast and pasta, which was great though I could have done without the sun-dried tomatoes they put in it. Items are a bit pricey but the final bill was just around $21, thanks to our passport unlimited discount. Would recommend this place if you're looking for a peaceful lunch. Doesn't seem to have a lot of visitors, seemingly hidden by the Holiday Inn hotel it's a part of.</review>< Rating>

< review>
Brought here by an in-law who doesn't know that I don't like hot dogs. I can't fault the restaurant for that. I looked for alternatives and found tater tots. Trying to eat healthy so kept looking and was happy I found Brussel sprouts. Hubby ordered while I saved a table so I didn't ask questions... like, "how long do you keep those beautiful little veggies deep in the fryer to remove any resemblance of a Brussel sprout?" :-(

I ended up picking them apart to find small pieces in the center of some that were not crisp beyond recognition.  I'd ordered chili also for some form of protein and found little chunks of hot dogs in it. Yuck!

Now, the rest of the family chowed down loved the food and had a great time but, if you want to eat even semi-healthy, I Do Not recommend this place.</review>

<userid>102567629828340282877</userid><username>Arthur Torres</username><Time>1614522424124</Time><Rating>5< /Rating>< Text>
I always stay in pacific groove,  and usually head towards the warm for food, but I couldn't resist trying this place because of the stars by other members, at first I wasn't sure because there was no one there at the time.  Upon entering you soon notice that this place has embraced a culture of California and made it truly one of a kind.  The food was probably the most simple ingredients yet so creative make your taste buds happy. Was cold out because of Covid-19 but they had heaters, they even have coffee, no ice cream this day, but they got it.   If I was a millionaire I totally would try to buy a franchise of this place.    Upon 5 min into our eat, the place got packed.  They got my order wrong offered to credit the extra food. But I was like nope ill be happy to buy another.   My favorite was the peeks, but destroying the other food next time.  This place needs to spread across California.< /Text>

<userid>104045590052261551519<//userid><Pictures>None<//Pictures>< review>
This place is excellent.

I stayed in Pacific Grove over a 3 day weekend. I visited Lucy's 4 times.

Their ice cream and shakes are amazing. The coffee is quite good as well.

However, it was the friendly staff that I appreciated the most. Morning or night everyone was courteous and gave off the vibe of people who actually enjoy their place of work. No McDrones here!

During one of my visits an elderly lady had a bad fall on the sidewalk outside that led to paramedics and police being called. She was checked over and was okay other than a nasty bump on the head.
I bring this up due to the response of the staff at Lucy's.
Once the hubbub died down and paramedics left the staff sat the woman down at a table. They took care of her order without payment and took some time to chat with her.

It made me very happy to see the care the staff took with this lady who had an unfortunate accident. Their conversation was very organic and sweet.

I'll definitely be returning to Pacific Grove in the future and Lucy's will be a required stop every time.< /review>

< Text>
An underrated place for relatively authentic Szechuan food! The owners are extremely friendly and welcoming. The restaurant itself is cozy and comfortable.

Make sure to try the cumin beef and iron pot offerings when you're here you won't regret it. Lots of great spicy food and a pretty long menu. It can be a bit pricey but not bad for the city. My wife and I have made this place our regular go-to for spicy Chinese food!

P.S. - it's not called tofu village anymore. It's called Szechuan Cuisine with a big red sign.</Text>

<user>104600150006171765694< /user><username>Sam Khandelwal<//username><date>1552675200600</date>< rate>
5</rate>
<review>NPR said, sichuan or Szechuan food is the next big cuisine to take over the planet. I believed them and decided to hunt for the best Sichuan restaurant. Exhibit A - voila - Szechuan cuisine.

What makes szechuan cuisine very interesting is a unique blend of spices. Not hot per se, but have this numbing sensation, that numbs your tongue, mouth, but in a pleasant way.

You can ask for the level of spice to be turned down - we didn't - and we survived to tell the tale.

The menu is overwhelming, over 100 items, some with photos, and strange sounding concoctions. But you can ask the server for recommendations (they are super friendly). I asked for veggie and seafood, and the wife wanted the best dim sums (they recommended pork in chili oil). We had tofu, shrimp and greens-based apps and entrees. You cannot go wrong - none of the 5 items we tried was a doozy.

Great flavors, no MSG, great service (yes, in an Asian restaurant), and food prepared with love - this is your destination du delicious jour.< /review><pictures>None< /pictures><Response>None<//Response><Gmap_id>0x8085876f88db7083:0x13532df4f8c514b3</Gmap_id></record></dataset><record>

They are always friendly & helpful! We moved to the area about 2 years ago & chose this location because it was indoors, not too far from home, has convenient hours, and it is clean. It took us a while to decide where to store our household goods since we moved into a smaller house from out-of-state.  We are very happy that we chose this location!  All of the storage facilities closer to our house were not climate controlled, cost more & usually drive-up type.  (We had a drive up storage in Spokane & although it can be easier, it was humid & musky even though it was a brand new facility. Plus we had so many bugs at that one!) When I signed up for this storage space at the end of 2011 it was the best deal in the area.  I haven't priced units recently so I don't know if the price is still competitive.
I have a space on the 3rd floor.  Sometimes I have problems accessing the elevator but it just means having to input my password 2 or 3 times.
The bathroom on the 3rd floor does not work - it has not worked since I moved in.
There are no trash cans available, either.
I understand Public Storage might be concerned about a) the customers destroying the restroom, and b) dealing with dumping problems, but isn't that part of the business?
Adie is the manager in the office and has been there since I began renting while all the other employees have come and gone.  I hope Public Storage is paying her a decent wage because she deserves it!< /text>
